{"id":1218624115,"title":"8213531: Test javax/swing/border/TestTitledBorderLeak.java fails","body":"Test was failing in linux citing `java.lang.RuntimeException: Expected Total TitledBorder to be freed : 10 Freed 9 `\r\nAs per the fix done in JDK-8204963 http://hg.openjdk.java.net/jdk/jdk/rev/cd7d2f9154fd\r\nthere was no platform specific code done for the fix and logs in `TitledBorder.installPropertyChangeListeners` shows it was called 10 times for the test but `CleanerFactory.cleaner().register` action was only called 9 times in linux causing it to fail.\r\n\r\nModified the test to not show the frame which cause the problem to go away and also it can still be used as 8204963 regression test as it still fails without the fix and pass with it. Modified test has passed in all platforms for several iterations.\r\n\r\nAlso removed the deprecated `System.runFinalization`\n\n<!-- Anything below this marker will be automatically updated, please do not edit manually! -->\n---------\n### Progress\n- [x] Change must not contain extraneous whitespace\n- [x] Commit message must refer to an issue\n- [ ] Change must be properly reviewed\n\n### Issue\n * [JDK-8213531](https://bugs.openjdk.java.net/browse/JDK-8213531): Test javax/swing/border/TestTitledBorderLeak.java fails\n\n\n### Reviewing\n<details><summary>Using <code>git<\/code><\/summary>\n\nCheckout this PR locally: \\\n`$ git fetch https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk pull/8450/head:pull/8450` \\\n`$ git checkout pull/8450`\n\nUpdate a local copy of the PR: \\\n`$ git checkout pull/8450` \\\n`$ git pull https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk pull/8450/head`\n\n<\/details>\n<details><summary>Using Skara CLI tools<\/summary>\n\nCheckout this PR locally: \\\n`$ git pr checkout 8450`\n\nView PR using the GUI difftool: \\\n`$ git pr show -t 8450`\n\n<\/details>\n<details><summary>Using diff file<\/summary>\n\nDownload this PR as a diff file: \\\n<a href=\"https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk/pull/8450.diff\">https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk/pull/8450.diff<\/a>\n\n<\/details>\n"}
{"id":772898511,"title":"AWT & Swing on Windows","body":"AWT & Swing are not currently supported on Windows. There are several aspects to adding this support, so the aim of this issue is to describe the overall approach. The actual work will be done under separate issues.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Linking with Native Libraries\r\n\r\nWhen it comes to linking, we considered both options: static and dynamic. However, initial testing (which was fairly basic) has already revealed problems with static linking that can't be reasonably solved without modifying the JDK (e.g., it affects the [static initialization order](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order) in such a way as to cause a segfault). On the other hand, dynamic linking allows us to reuse native libraries as they are.\r\n\r\nTherefore, the plan is to add support for dynamic linking, as there are fewer unknowns.\r\n\r\nWork is currently in progress: #3085\r\n\r\n\r\n### Swing\r\n\r\nNative images currently have `java.home` set to `null`. This is problematic as the Swing code assumes the existence and layout of the `java.home` directory in order to load various configurations. So to avoid Swing substitutions, we need a real directory with the expected layout and content.\r\n\r\nThe plan is to set `java.home` to the directory from which the native image is executed.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Build Output\r\n\r\nBoth dynamic linking and Swing support imply that the output of a native image build will no longer be a single binary, but multiple binaries or even a whole directory.\r\n\r\nThe current plan is to put everything next to the built native image, which should be enough to enable proper functioning. Later, we could introduce some configurability and / or support to bundle everything into a zip archive.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Build Configuration\r\n\r\nCurrently, the use of `native-image-agent` ([see documentation](https://github.com/oracle/graal/blob/master/substratevm/BuildConfiguration.md#assisted-configuration-of-native-image-builds)) is required even in the most trivial cases. And while this should be possible to improve, at this point it is difficult to say to what extent.\r\n\r\nThe rough idea is to provide AWT & Swing configurations out of the box where possible.\r\n"}

{"id":772898511,"title":"AWT & Swing on Windows","body":"AWT & Swing are not currently supported on Windows. There are several aspects to adding this support, so the aim of this issue is to describe the overall approach. The actual work will be done under separate issues.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Linking with Native Libraries\r\n\r\nWhen it comes to linking, we considered both options: static and dynamic. However, initial testing (which was fairly basic) has already revealed problems with static linking that can't be reasonably solved without modifying the JDK (e.g., it affects the [static initialization order](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order) in such a way as to cause a segfault). On the other hand, dynamic linking allows us to reuse native libraries as they are.\r\n\r\nTherefore, the plan is to add support for dynamic linking, as there are fewer unknowns.\r\n\r\nWork is currently in progress: #3085\r\n\r\n\r\n### Swing\r\n\r\nNative images currently have `java.home` set to `null`. This is problematic as the Swing code assumes the existence and layout of the `java.home` directory in order to load various configurations. So to avoid Swing substitutions, we need a real directory with the expected layout and content.\r\n\r\nThe plan is to set `java.home` to the directory from which the native image is executed.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Build Output\r\n\r\nBoth dynamic linking and Swing support imply that the output of a native image build will no longer be a single binary, but multiple binaries or even a whole directory.\r\n\r\nThe current plan is to put everything next to the built native image, which should be enough to enable proper functioning. Later, we could introduce some configurability and / or support to bundle everything into a zip archive.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Build Configuration\r\n\r\nCurrently, the use of `native-image-agent` ([see documentation](https://github.com/oracle/graal/blob/master/substratevm/BuildConfiguration.md#assisted-configuration-of-native-image-builds)) is required even in the most trivial cases. And while this should be possible to improve, at this point it is difficult to say to what extent.\r\n\r\nThe rough idea is to provide AWT & Swing configurations out of the box where possible.\r\n"}

{"id":1229511548,"title":"Use kotlinx-coroutines for UI launcher","body":"## Description\r\n\r\nThis PR moves `startGui` from `class JMeter` to another class.\r\n\r\n## Motivation and Context\r\n\r\na) It is nice to factor UI from non-UI code\r\nb) Current code fails to update progress during \"GUI startup\". The reason is that all the contents of `startGui` is running in a single `Runnable`, so Swing has no way to break in-between and render progress updates.\r\nSee https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=66044#c5\r\n\r\nCoroutines enable an easy-to-maintain approach for splitting long UI methods into chunks.\r\nIn this case, I used `yield()` right after `setProgress`, so we give room for the Swing event dispatcher thread to update the UI.\r\n\r\nSee also https://github.com/Kotlin/kotlinx.coroutines/blob/master/ui/coroutines-guide-ui.md\r\n\r\n## Checklist:\r\n<!--- Go over all the following points, and put an `x` in all the boxes that apply. -->\r\n<!--- If you're unsure about any of these, don't hesitate to ask. We're here to help! -->\r\n- [x] My code follows the [code style][style-guide] of this project.\r\n- [ ] I have updated the documentation accordingly.\r\n\r\n[style-guide]: https://wiki.apache.org/jmeter/CodeStyleGuidelines\r\n"}

{"id":1221787757,"title":"[PATCH] Avoid redundant HashMap.containsKey calls in NimbusDefaults","body":"The method `javax.swing.plaf.nimbus.NimbusDefaults#getDerivedColor(String,String,float,float,float,int,boolean)` could be improved by usage of Map.putIfAbsent instead of separate `containsKey`/`get`/`put` calls. We known that HashMap `javax.swing.plaf.nimbus.NimbusDefaults#derivedColors` can contain only non-null values. And to check if `putIfAbsent` was successful or not, we can just compare result with `null`.\r\nIt makes code a bit cleaner and faster.\n\n<!-- Anything below this marker will be automatically updated, please do not edit manually! -->\n---------\n### Progress\n- [x] Change must not contain extraneous whitespace\n- [ ] Commit message must refer to an issue\n- [ ] Change must be properly reviewed\n\n### Reviewing\n<details><summary>Using <code>git<\/code><\/summary>\n\nCheckout this PR locally: \\\n`$ git fetch https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk pull/8482/head:pull/8482` \\\n`$ git checkout pull/8482`\n\nUpdate a local copy of the PR: \\\n`$ git checkout pull/8482` \\\n`$ git pull https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk pull/8482/head`\n\n<\/details>\n<details><summary>Using Skara CLI tools<\/summary>\n\nCheckout this PR locally: \\\n`$ git pr checkout 8482`\n\nView PR using the GUI difftool: \\\n`$ git pr show -t 8482`\n\n<\/details>\n<details><summary>Using diff file<\/summary>\n\nDownload this PR as a diff file: \\\n<a href=\"https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk/pull/8482.diff\">https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk/pull/8482.diff<\/a>\n\n<\/details>\n"}

{"id":1191115550,"title":"OptionsLookAndFeel: Support for FlatLaf","body":"@ctrueden, this PR is a proposal on how [Flatlaf](https://github.com/JFormDesigner/FlatLaf#flatlaf---flat-look-and-feel) could be used as an _optional_ L&F for Swing components in Fiji/SciJava in direct response to #61. The advantages of FlatLaf L&Fs are discussed in #61, and  include:\r\n- Proper hiDPI scaling under Java 8 (this is mainly relevant to linux nowadays, but still relevant to other OSes: e.g., Native L&F on the mac scales everything without judgment, and so margins and borders become awkwardly exaggerated: this does not happen with FlatFlaf)\r\n- Much more modern and polished 'feel' relative to JVM default options\r\n- Several fixes for current Swing bugs and limitations that will not be fixed upstream\r\n- Many improvements like[ improved submenu navigation](https://github.com/JFormDesigner/FlatLaf/releases/tag/2.1)\r\n- Dark themes, that have been asked several times, e.g., in the script editor [here](https://forum.image.sc/t/shiny-new-script-editor/64160/37?u=tferr), and [here](https://github.com/scijava/script-editor/pull/56#issuecomment-1050888837)\r\n\r\nThis PR also includes a  static method so that Look and Feel can be set more easily at startup. E.g., for Fjii the following\r\ncall in the StartupMacros could now be used to set the Look and Feel programmatically:\r\n```\r\neval(\"js\",\"importClass(Packages.org.scijava.ui.swing.options.OptionsLookAndFeel);OptionsLookAndFeel.setupLookAndFeel('FlatLaf Dark');\") \r\n```\r\nA couple of notes:\r\n- The flatlaf dependency is now being declared in this pom. I assume it should be declared in the parent pom-scijava? I imagine multiple releases of components would be needed, so if you don't mind I would pass that work onto you\r\n- If this gets merged, dark themes in Fiji would still remain problematic. In addition to the obvious fact that  java.awt components will not change, there are currently some hardwired colors in several components (e.g., Console) that would need to be patched for dark themes to work properly. One would need to remove/adjust explicit `setColor()` references in the code. I am not doing that here, in case there are technical issues with adopting third-party L&F libraries that I am not foreseeing, and this cannot be merged.\r\n- I would actually vote for FlatLaf to be the default in Fiji (for the reasons above). However, on the Mac AWT and Swing are too intertwined, and currently choosing a flatlaf theme on MacOS, makes some components of the GenericDialog loose rounded edges. So it may be wise for the time being to consider the possibility of having it as a default only on Windows and Linux. I will open an issue there to see if this can be fixed."}

{"id":1048430859,"title":"Made StatusBar swing timer stoppable","body":"### Description of the Change\r\n\r\nIn the class gov.nasa.worldwind.util.StatusBar a SwingTimer is created as a local variable in the constructor. This way the timer can never be stopped.\r\n\r\n### Why Should This Be In Core?\r\n\r\nEvery Application which does not rely on System.exit() for its shutdown could have a problem with the timer mentioned above as the AWT Thread won't stop. Usage of System.exit() can be a problem if there are automated system tests executed by tools like the maven-failsafe-plugin, which does not allow for such calls.\r\n\r\n### Benefits\r\n\r\nThe timer can be stopped and applications can do a graceful shutdown.\r\n\r\n### Potential Drawbacks\r\n\r\nThere is the risk that a programmer calls the stop method and wonders why the network status is not updated anymore. It could even be argued that the encapsulation is broken but by using global state like the swing timer facility there is no other practical way to clean this up the way it is currently designed.\r\n\r\n### Applicable Issues"}

options:\r\n\r\n```java\r\nOptions.v().set_verbose(false);\r\nOptions.v().set_whole_program(true);\r\nOptions.v().set_app(true);\r\nOptions.v().set_allow_phantom_refs(true);\r\nOptions.v().set_output_format(Options.output_format_class);\r\nOptions.v().setPhaseOption(\"jb\", \"enabled:false\");\r\n// Enable SPARK\r\nOptions.v().setPhaseOption(\"cg.spark\", \"enabled:true\");\r\nOptions.v().setPhaseOption(\"cg.spark\", \"verbose:true\");\r\nOptions.v().setPhaseOption(\"cg.spark\", \"on-fly-cg:true\");\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe following test application, when analyzed using soot 4.2.1, provides a callgraph which extends back through to the `actionPerformed` methods in the `ActionListener`s:\r\n\r\n```java\r\nimport javax.swing.JFrame;\r\nimport javax.swing.JButton;\r\nimport java.awt.event.ActionEvent;\r\nimport java.awt.event.ActionListener;\r\n\r\n\r\npublic class TinyUI\r\n{\r\n    public class Printer implements ActionListener\r\n    {\r\n        public void actionPerformed( final ActionEvent e )\r\n        {\r\n            System.out.println(\"printing\");\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    public class Quitter implements ActionListener\r\n    {\r\n        public void actionPerformed( final ActionEvent e )\r\n        {\r\n            System.exit(0);\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    public static void main( final String[] args )\r\n    {\r\n        final JFrame frame = new JFrame();\r\n        frame.setSize( 400, 500 );\r\n        frame.setLayout( null );\r\n        frame.setVisible( true );\r\n\r\n        final JButton printButton = new JButton( \"print\" );\r\n        printButton.addActionListener( new TinyUI().new Printer() );\r\n        printButton.setBounds( 10, 10, 100, 100 );\r\n        frame.add( printButton );\r\n\r\n        final JButton quitButton = new JButton( \"quit\" );\r\n        quitButton.addActionListener( new TinyUI().new Quitter() );\r\n        quitButton.setBounds( 10, 200, 100, 100 );\r\n        frame.add( quitButton );\r\n    }\r\n\r\n    private static void DebloatThisFunction() {}\r\n}\r\n```\r\nUsing soot 4.3.0, the callgraph does not extend to the `ActionListener`s, e.g. `TinyUI$Printer: void actionPerformed(java.awt.event.ActionEvent)`.\r\n\r\n**Reproduction**\r\nWe examine the callgraph with the following code:\r\n```java\r\nCallGraph cg = Scene.v().getCallGraph();\r\n```\r\n**Expected**\r\nFrom a high level the \"correct\" callgraph should, at least, include a connection back to these `actionPerformed` methods.  I have done a relatively extensive tracing through the 4.2.1 and 4.3.0 callgraphs and, due to the complexity of these swing event handlers, it's a little unclear what _correct_ would actually look like.  In essence, the major problem is that there is no connection between the backend framework and this test code in 4.3.0.\r\n\r\n**Stacktrace**\r\nWhile there is no stacktrace, these are notes that I've collected while trying to debug this:\r\n* Soot output:\r\n    `[ERROR] Failed Typing in <java.awt.image.ComponentColorModel: int getRGBComponent(int,int)> at statement l3#1 = $r0: Is not cast compatible: null_type <-- java.lang.Object`\r\n* 4.3.0 does not have a `doClick()` in the callgraph. (exists in 4.2.1)\r\n* Adding a programmatic `doClick()` in `main()` generates a callgraph connection to both `actionPerformed` methods. \r\n* 4.3.0 callgraph does not contain `getColorModel` which should be a JButton method.  (exists in 4.2.1)\r\n* It's possible that the methods \"after\" `getColorModel` are not properly processed when generating the callgraph.\r\n* The EventListener framework appears to be dropped from the callgraph in 4.3.0.\r\n\r\n**Additional context**\r\nWe would like to help continue debugging this issue so any advice would be appreciated.  My current theory is that the processing of JComponent fails, potentially where the typing failure happens, and additional critical methods are \"dropped\" from the scene.\r\n\r\nI will post a followup code sample that isolates the `not cast compatible: null_type` error."}

{"id":543716007,"title":"Feature/#2908 swing ui improvements","body":"Fixes #2908 \r\nFixes #2836 \r\nFixes #2825 \r\nFixes #2469 \r\nFixes #1880\r\n\r\nThis is a large change to the structure of the Swing interface so I've created a feature branch for it so it can be tested a bit more extensively.  The ZK interface has not been affected.\r\n\r\nFeature wise, it changes the look and feel of the swing editors, making them act consistently in forms and the table.  The table can freeze columns similar to a spreadsheet.  When a field has the focus, in the form or table, typing will start editing the field.  The Enter key will stop editing and commit the change.  The Escape key will revert the change to the field.  The tab key will stop editing, commit the change and move to the next field.\r\n\r\nIn a form, when not editing a field, the Enter key will act on the button that has the focus or the default button if no button has the focus.  In the table, the Enter key or shift Enter will move the focus\r\nup and down.  Tab will cycle the focus to the right. Shift tab will cycle to the left.  The Home and End key will move the focus to the first or last cell in the row.\r\n\r\nIn the form, F2 will create a new record but in the table F2 will start editing a field.  To create a new record in the table, click Ctrl-F2.\r\n\r\nThe combo box has been changed to use a more flexible form of auto-completion and auto-reduction.  The popup will appear and show entries that have a partial match to the typed text.  For example \"li\" will match Eng**li**sh and Ita**li**ano.  Typing Enter will select the highlighted choice.  Enter again will commit the change.\r\n\r\nEscaping or ignoring a change with the Escape key will first revert the change to the field being edited and stop the editor.  If no field is being edited, the Escape key will revert the changes to any other field since the last commit of the record.  This helps when entering data where a mistake is made.  Previously, the Escape key would wipe the entire record, deleting all the other fields as well.  Now, the user can just revert the one field with one click of Escape or the entire record with two clicks of Escape.\r\n\r\nThe delete key will delete the contents of the field that has the focus.\r\n\r\nThe Date field will show a light grey hint when it has the focus as an editor and a null value.  The hint will use the date format applied.\r\n\r\nIn the table, right clicking in the header will show a pop-up that can be used to hide columns or freeze columns.  If Freeze is selected, all the columns to the left will be frozen in place.  Sizing of the frozen columns in not possible but the rest of the table can be manipulated as required.  The focus moves seamlessly between the frozen columns and the main table.  Right click in the header again to unfreeze the columns.\r\n\r\nThe way columns are hidden has been changed so that the columns are removed from the table view model.  This allows focus to move cleanly around that table.  Previously, the hidden columns existed in the view but were not shown, resulting in the focus disapearing when a hidden columns was selected.\r\n\r\nThe cell renderers and cell editors use the same representation as the form.  The method of testing the context for dynamic display uses the table or context as required to provide the same functionality whether in the form or table.\r\n\r\nIn separating the Swing interface from the Base classes, there are several cases where public methods that returned swing classes have been moved to the Client.  Where possible I deprecated these changes but it wasn't possible in all cases.\r\n\r\nThe Swing PLAF files have been moved to the Client and I've added UI elements for most of the editors.  This speeds up their creation a fair bit as all the UI setup was being done twice.  The way the editor are displayed is more consistent and appear similar to the ComboBox.  Behind the scenes an abstract editor now contains most of the editor code and an abstract UI element handles most of the common UI appearance.  This has reduced the complexity and amount of duplicated code  quite a bit.\r\n\r\nI really enjoy using the new interface compared to the previous one and I hope you do as well.\r\n"}

{"id":1213766150,"title":"[BUG] Java Admin Client uses non-Swing concurrency to interact with GUI","body":"The Java Admin Client is a Swing application, and as such should follow the Swing guidelines when using multiple threads to update UI components. See - https://docs.oracle.com/javase/tutorial/uiswing/concurrency/index.html\r\n\r\nTherefore we should modify the existing background tasks that use Runnable's and calls to `InteractiveClient#newClientThread(String, Runnable)` with instances of `SwingWorker`.\r\n\r\nThis also has the benefit of giving us the facility to incrementally update the UI as chunks of results become available.\r\n\r\nFor an example of how to do this, see - https://github.com/eXist-db/exist/pull/4356/commits/e3c834e0c965a7f97af106e00529ef18089984cd"}

{"id":73047671,"title":"Standard Swing Inheritance Patterns","body":"```\nThis library looks *amazing* and would dramatically improve the quality of many \nJava apps. I find myself lusting after many of these widgets because there are \nsimply no satisfying alternatives in Swing or SwingX.\n\nHowever, although I understand the sentiment and simplicity of use for your \nAPI, your widgets do not follow the same bean pattern as core Swing components. \nThis means that GUI Editors - such as the Netbeans one - cannot use your \nwidgets.\n\nPlease release a version which has Swing style patterns so that they can be \ndrag and dropped into Netbeans GUI Editor.\n```\n\nOriginal issue reported on code.google.com by `Sam.Hall...@gmail.com` on 31 May 2012 at 10:07\n"}
{"id":109697887,"title":"Standard Swing Inheritance Patterns","body":"```\nThis library looks *amazing* and would dramatically improve the quality of many \nJava apps. I find myself lusting after many of these widgets because there are \nsimply no satisfying alternatives in Swing or SwingX.\n\nHowever, although I understand the sentiment and simplicity of use for your \nAPI, your widgets do not follow the same bean pattern as core Swing components. \nThis means that GUI Editors - such as the Netbeans one - cannot use your \nwidgets.\n\nPlease release a version which has Swing style patterns so that they can be \ndrag and dropped into Netbeans GUI Editor.\n```\n\nOriginal issue reported on code.google.com by `Sam.Hall...@gmail.com` on 31 May 2012 at 10:07\n"}

{"id":100878361,"title":"Standard Swing Inheritance Patterns","body":"```\nThis library looks *amazing* and would dramatically improve the quality of many \nJava apps. I find myself lusting after many of these widgets because there are \nsimply no satisfying alternatives in Swing or SwingX.\n\nHowever, although I understand the sentiment and simplicity of use for your \nAPI, your widgets do not follow the same bean pattern as core Swing components. \nThis means that GUI Editors - such as the Netbeans one - cannot use your \nwidgets.\n\nPlease release a version which has Swing style patterns so that they can be \ndrag and dropped into Netbeans GUI Editor.\n```\n\nOriginal issue reported on code.google.com by `Sam.Hall...@gmail.com` on 31 May 2012 at 10:07\n"}

{"id":60998501,"title":"Standard Swing Inheritance Patterns","body":"```\nThis library looks *amazing* and would dramatically improve the quality of many \nJava apps. I find myself lusting after many of these widgets because there are \nsimply no satisfying alternatives in Swing or SwingX.\n\nHowever, although I understand the sentiment and simplicity of use for your \nAPI, your widgets do not follow the same bean pattern as core Swing components. \nThis means that GUI Editors - such as the Netbeans one - cannot use your \nwidgets.\n\nPlease release a version which has Swing style patterns so that they can be \ndrag and dropped into Netbeans GUI Editor.\n```\n\nOriginal issue reported on code.google.com by `Sam.Hall...@gmail.com` on 31 May 2012 at 10:07\n"}

{"id":99890926,"title":"Standard Swing Inheritance Patterns","body":"```\nThis library looks *amazing* and would dramatically improve the quality of many \nJava apps. I find myself lusting after many of these widgets because there are \nsimply no satisfying alternatives in Swing or SwingX.\n\nHowever, although I understand the sentiment and simplicity of use for your \nAPI, your widgets do not follow the same bean pattern as core Swing components. \nThis means that GUI Editors - such as the Netbeans one - cannot use your \nwidgets.\n\nPlease release a version which has Swing style patterns so that they can be \ndrag and dropped into Netbeans GUI Editor.\n```\n\nOriginal issue reported on code.google.com by `Sam.Hall...@gmail.com` on 31 May 2012 at 10:07\n"}

{"id":960493693,"title":"javax.swing.ImageIcon classloader leak","body":"The class `javax.swing.ImageIcon` causes a classloader leak which is not covered yet by default (as of classloader-leak-prevention 2.7.0).\r\n\r\nSteps to reproduce:\r\n1. Build the attached example project [imageicon-leak.zip](https://github.com/mjiderhamn/classloader-leak-prevention/files/6931705/imageicon-leak.zip) (mvn clean install)\r\n2. Deploy the .war file into a Tomcat 8.5.65\r\n3. Undeploy it again\r\n\r\nThen the classloader is not garbage collected due to the following Path2GC:\r\n![imageicon-leak](https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/25172174/128191807-da873687-f67f-4df9-afd2-487f644fa575.png)\r\n\r\nObviously the instance of the anonymous class `javax.swing.ImageIcon$3` has a reference to an `AccessControlContext` retaining the `ParallelWebappClassLoader`. It is created at ImageIcon.java line 347 (from AdoptOpenJDK jdk8u272-b10):\r\n```java\r\n    private MediaTracker getTracker() {\r\n        Object trackerObj;\r\n        AppContext ac = AppContext.getAppContext();\r\n        // Opt: Only synchronize if trackerObj comes back null?\r\n        // If null, synchronize, re-check for null, and put new tracker\r\n        synchronized(ac) {\r\n            trackerObj = ac.get(TRACKER_KEY);\r\n            if (trackerObj == null) {\r\n                Component comp = new Component() {};   // <--- javax.swing.ImageIcon$3\r\n                trackerObj = new MediaTracker(comp);\r\n                ac.put(TRACKER_KEY, trackerObj);\r\n            }\r\n        }\r\n        return (MediaTracker) trackerObj;\r\n    }\r\n```\r\n\r\nAdding the following clean-up step solves this issue:\r\n\r\n```java\r\npublic class AwtMediaTrackerCleanUp implements ClassLoaderPreMortemCleanUp {\r\n\r\n    @Override\r\n    public void cleanUp(ClassLoaderLeakPreventor preventor) {\r\n        StringBuilder trackerKey = preventor.getStaticFieldValue(ImageIcon.class, \"TRACKER_KEY\");\r\n        AppContext appContext = AppContext.getAppContext();\r\n        synchronized (appContext) {\r\n            appContext.remove(trackerKey);\r\n        }\r\n    }\r\n}\r\n```"}
